publishes records to the Kafka cluster.\n   102→ * <P>\n   103→ * The producer is <i>thread safe</i> and sharing a single producer instance across threads will generally be faster than\n   104→ * having multiple instances.\n   105→ * <p>\n   106→ * Here is a simple example of using the producer to send records with strings containing sequential numbers as the key/value\n   107→ * pairs.\n   108→ * <pre>\n   109→ * {@code\n   110→ * Properties props = new Properties();\n   111→ * props.put(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\n   112→ * props.put(\"linger.ms\", 1);\n   113→ * props.put(\"key.serializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer\");\n   114→ * props.put(\"value.serializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringSerializer\");\n   115→ *\n   116→ * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props);\n   117→ * for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++)\n   118→ *     producer.send(new ProducerRecord<String, String>(\"my-topic\", Integer.toString(i), Integer.toString(i)));\n   119→ *\n   120→ * producer.close();\n   121→ * }</pre>\n   122→ * <p>\n   123→ * The producer consists of a pool of buffer space that holds records that haven't yet been transmitted to the server\n   124→ * as well as a background I/O thread that is responsible for turning these records into requests and transmitting them\n   125→ * to the cluster. Failure to close the producer after use will leak these resources.\n   126→ * <p>\n   127→ * The {@link #send(ProducerRecord) send()} method is asynchronous. When called, it adds the record to a buffer of pending record sends\n   128→ * and immediately returns. This allows the producer to batch together individual records for efficiency.\n   129→ * <p>\n   130→ * The <code>acks</code> config controls the criteria under which requests are considered complete. The default setting \"all\"\n   131→ * will result in blocking on the full commit of the record, the slowest but most durable setting.\n   132→ * <p>\n   133→ * If the request fails, the producer can automatically retry. The <code>retries</code> setting defaults to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>, and\n   134→ * it's recommended to use <code>delivery.timeout.ms</code> to control retry behavior, instead of <code>retries</code>.\n   135→ * <p>\n   136→ * The producer maintains buffers of unsent records for each partition. These buffers are of a size specified by\n   137→ * the <code>batch.size</code> config. Making this larger can result in more batching, but requires more memory (since we will\n   138→ * generally have one of these buffers for each active partition).\n   139→ * <p>\n   140→ * By default a buffer is available to send immediately even if there is additional unused space in the buffer. However if you\n   141→ * want to reduce the number of requests you can set <code>linger.ms</code> to something greater than 0. This will\n   142→ * instruct the producer to wait up to that number of milliseconds before sending a request in hope that more records will\n   143→ * arrive to fill up the same batch. This is analogous to Nagle's algorithm in TCP. For example, in the code snippet above,\n   144→ * likely all 100 records would be sent in a single request since we set our linger time to 1 millisecond. However this setting\n   145→ * would add 1 millisecond of latency to our request waiting for more records to arrive if we didn't fill up the buffer. Note that\n   146→ * records that arrive close together in time will generally batch together even with <code>linger.ms=0</code>. So, under heavy load,\n   147→ * batching will occur regardless of the linger configuration; however setting this to something larger than 0 can lead to fewer, more\n   148→ * efficient requests when not under maximal load at the cost of a small amount of latency.\n   149→ * <p>\n   150→ * The <code>buffer.memory</code> controls the total amount of memory available to the producer for buffering. java.util.Set;\n    48→import java.util.regex.Pattern;\n    49→\n    50→import static org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Utils.propsToMap;\n    51→\n    52→/**\n    53→ * A client that consumes records from a Kafka cluster.\n    54→ * <p>\n    55→ * This client transparently handles the failure of Kafka brokers, and transparently adapts as topic partitions\n    56→ * it fetches migrate within the cluster. This client also interacts with the broker to allow groups of\n    57→ * consumers to load balance consumption using <a href=\"#consumergroups\">consumer groups</a>.\n    58→ * <p>\n    59→ * The consumer maintains TCP connections to the necessary brokers to fetch data.\n    60→ * Failure to close the consumer after use will leak these connections.\n    61→ * The consumer is not thread-safe. See <a href=\"#multithreaded\">Multi-threaded Processing</a> for more details.\n    62→ *\n    63→ * <h3>Cross-Version Compatibility</h3>\n    64→ * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\n    65→ * certain features. For example, 0.10.0 brokers do not support offsetsForTimes, because this feature was added\n    66→ * in version 0.10.1. You will receive an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException}\n    67→ * when invoking an API that is not available on the running broker version.\n    68→ * <p>\n    69→ *\n    70→ * <h3>Offsets and Consumer Position</h3>\n    71→ * Kafka maintains a numerical offset for each record in a partition. This offset acts as a unique identifier of\n    72→ * a record within that partition, and also denotes the position of the consumer in the partition. For example, a consumer\n    73→ * which is at position 5 has consumed records with offsets 0 through 4 and will next receive the record with offset 5.\n    74→ * Note that offsets are not guaranteed to be consecutive (such as compacted topic or when records have been produced\n    75→ * using transactions). For example, if the consumer did read a record with offset 4, but 5 is not an offset\n    76→ * with a record, its position might advance to 6 (or higher) directly. Similarly, if the consumer's position is 5,\n    77→ * but there is no record with offset 5, the consumer will return the record with the next higher offset.\n    78→ * There are actually two notions of position relevant to the user of the consumer:\n    79→ * <p>\n    80→ * The {@link #position(TopicPartition) position} of the consumer gives the offset of the next record that will be given\n    81→ * out. It will be one larger than the highest offset the consumer has seen in that partition. It automatically advances\n    82→ * every time the consumer receives messages in a call to {@link #poll(Duration)}.\n    83→ * <p>\n    84→ * The {@link #commitSync() committed position} is the last offset that has been stored securely. Should the\n    85→ * process fail and restart, this is the offset that the consumer will recover to. The consumer can either automatically commit\n    86→ * offsets periodically; or it can choose to control this committed position manually by calling one of the commit APIs\n    87→ * (e.g. {@link #commitSync() commitSync} and {@link #commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback) commitAsync}).\n    88→ * <p>\n    89→ * This distinction gives the consumer control over when a record is considered consumed. It is discussed in further\n    90→ * detail below.\n    91→ *\n    92→ * <h3><a name=\"consumergroups\">Consumer Groups and Topic Subscriptions</a></h3>\n    93→ *\n    94→ * Kafka uses the concept of <i>consumer groups</i> to allow a pool of processes to divide the work of consuming and\n    95→ * processing records. These processes can either be running on the same machine or they can be\n    96→ * distributed over many machines to provide scalability and fault tolerance for processing. All consumer instances\n    97→ * sharing the same {@code group.id} will be part of the same consumer group.\n    98→ * <p>\n    99→ * Each consumer in a group can dynamically set the list of topics it wants to subscribe to through one of the\n   100→ * {@link #subscribe(Collection, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribe} APIs. Kafka will deliver each message in the\n   101→ * subscribed topics to one process in each consumer group. This is achieved by balancing the partitions between all\n   102→ * members in the consumer group so that each partition is assigned to exactly one consumer in the group. So if there\n   103→ * is a topic with four partitions, and a consumer group with two processes, each process would consume from two partitions.\n   104→ * <p>\n   105→ * Membership in a consumer group is maintained dynamically: if a process fails, the partitions assigned to it will\n   106→ * be reassigned to other consumers in the same group. Similarly, if a new consumer joins the group, partitions will be moved\n   107→ * from existing consumers to the new one. This is known as <i>rebalancing</i> the group and is discussed in more\n   108→ * detail <a href=\"#failuredetection\">below</a>. Group rebalancing is also used when new partitions are added\n   109→ * to one of the subscribed topics or when a new topic matching a {@link #subscribe(Pattern, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribed regex}\n   110→ * is created. The group will automatically detect the new partitions through periodic metadata refreshes and\n   111→ * assign them to members of the group.\n   112→ * <p>\n   113→ * Conceptually you can think of a consumer group as being a single logical subscriber that happens to be made up of\n   114→ * multiple processes. As a multi-subscriber system, Kafka naturally supports having any number of consumer groups for a\n   115→ * given topic without duplicating data (additional consumers are actually quite cheap).\n   116→ * <p>\n   117→ * This is a slight generalization of the functionality that is common in messaging systems. To get semantics similar to\n   118→ * a queue in a traditional messaging system all processes would be part of a single consumer group and hence record\n   119→ * delivery would be balanced over the group like with a queue. Unlike a traditional messaging system, though, you can\n   120→ * have multiple such groups. To get semantics similar to pub-sub in a traditional messaging system each process would\n   121→ * have its own consumer group, so each process would subscribe to all the records published to the topic.\n   122→ * <p>\n   123→ * In addition, when group reassignment happens automatically, consumers can be notified through a {@link ConsumerRebalanceListener},\n   124→ * which allows them to finish necessary application-level logic such as state cleanup, manual offset\n   125→ * commits, etc. See <a href=\"#rebalancecallback\">Storing Offsets Outside Kafka</a> for more details.\n   126→ * <p>\n   127→ * It is also possible for the consumer to <a href=\"#manualassignment\">manually assign</a> specific partitions\n   128→ * (similar to the older \"simple\" consumer) using {@link #assign(Collection)}. In this case, dynamic partition\n   129→ * assignment and consumer group coordination will be disabled.\n   130→ *\n   131→ * <h3><a name=\"failuredetection\">Detecting Consumer Failures</a></h3>\n   132→ *\n   133→ * After subscribing to a set of topics, the consumer will automatically join the group when {@link #poll(Duration)} is\n   134→ * invoked. The poll API is designed to ensure consumer liveness. As long as you continue to call poll, the consumer\n   135→ * will stay in the group and continue to receive messages from the partitions it was assigned. Underneath the covers,\n   136→ * the consumer sends periodic heartbeats to the server. If the consumer crashes or is unable to send heartbeats for\n   137→ * a duration of {@code session.timeout.ms}, then the consumer will be considered dead and its partitions will\n   138→ * be reassigned.\n   139→ * <p>\n   140→ * It is also possible that the consumer could encounter a \"livelock\" situation where it is continuing\n   141→ * to send heartbeats, but no progress is being made. To prevent the consumer from holding onto its partitions\n   142→ * indefinitely in this case, we provide a liveness detection mechanism using the {@code max.poll.interval.ms}\n   143→ * setting. Basically if you don't call poll at least as frequently as the configured max interval,\n   144→ * then the client will proactively leave the group so that another consumer can take over its partitions. When this happens,\n   145→ * you may see an offset commit failure (as indicated by a {@link CommitFailedException} thrown from a call to {@link #commitSync()}).\n   146→ * This is a safety mechanism which guarantees that only active members of the group are able to commit offsets.\n   147→ * So to stay in the group, you must continue to call poll.\n   148→ * <p>\n   149→ * The consumer provides two configuration settings to control the behavior of the poll loop:\n   150→ * <ol>\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. org.apache.flink.core.io.InputStatus;\n    25→import org.apache.flink.metrics.Gauge;\n    26→import org.apache.flink.metrics.groups.OperatorIOMetricGroup;\n    27→import org.apache.flink.metrics.groups.SourceReaderMetricGroup;\n    28→\n    29→import java.util.Collection;\n    30→import java.util.List;\n    31→import java.util.concurrent.CompletableFuture;\n    32→\n    33→/**\n    34→ * The interface for a source reader which is responsible for reading the records from the source\n    35→ * splits assigned by {@link SplitEnumerator}.\n    36→ *\n    37→ * <p>For most non-trivial source reader, it is recommended to use {@link\n    38→ * org.apache.flink.connector.base.source.reader.SourceReaderBase SourceReaderBase} which provides\n    39→ * an efficient hand-over protocol to avoid blocking I/O inside the task thread and supports various\n    40→ * split-threading models.\n    41→ *\n    42→ * <p>Implementations can provide the following metrics:\n    43→ *\n    44→ * <ul>\n    45→ *   <li>{@link OperatorIOMetricGroup#getNumRecordsInCounter()} (highly recommended)\n    46→ *   <li>{@link OperatorIOMetricGroup#getNumBytesInCounter()} (recommended)\n    47→ *   <li>{@link SourceReaderMetricGroup#getNumRecordsInErrorsCounter()} (recommended)\n    48→ *   <li>{@link SourceReaderMetricGroup#setPendingRecordsGauge(Gauge)}\n    49→ *   <li>{@link SourceReaderMetricGroup#setPendingBytesGauge(Gauge)}\n    50→ * </ul>\n    51→ *\n    52→ * @param <T> The type of the record emitted by this source reader.\n    53→ * @param <SplitT> The type of the source splits.\n    54→ */\n    55→@Public\n    56→public interface SourceReader<T, SplitT extends SourceSplit>\n    57→        extends AutoCloseable, CheckpointListener {\n    58→\n    59→    /** Start the reader. */\n    60→    void start();\n    61→\n    62→    /**\n    63→     * Poll the next available record into the {@link ReaderOutput}.\n    64→     *\n    65→     * <p>The implementation must make sure this method is non-blocking.\n    66→     *\n    67→     * <p>Although the implementation can emit multiple records into the given ReaderOutput, it is\n    68→     * recommended not doing so. Instead, emit one record into the ReaderOutput and return a {@link\n    69→     * InputStatus#MORE_AVAILABLE} to let the caller thread know there are more records available.\n    70→     *\n    71→     * @return The InputStatus of the SourceReader after the method invocation.\n    72→     */\n    73→    InputStatus pollNext(ReaderOutput<T> output) throws Exception;\n    74→\n    75→    /**\n    76→     * Checkpoint on the state of the source.\n    77→     *\n    78→     * @return the state of the source.\n    79→     */\n    80→    List<SplitT> snapshotState(long checkpointId);\n    81→\n    82→    /**\n    83→     * Returns a future that signals that data is available from the reader.\n    84→     *\n    85→     * <p>Once the future completes, the runtime will keep calling the {@link\n    86→     * #pollNext(ReaderOutput)} method until that method returns a status other than {@link\n    87→     * InputStatus#MORE_AVAILABLE}. After that, the runtime will again call this method to obtain\n    88→     * the next future. Once that completes, it will again call {@link #pollNext(ReaderOutput)} and\n    89→     * so on.\n    90→     *\n    91→     * <p>The contract is the following: If the reader has data available, then all futures\n    92→     * previously returned by this method must eventually complete. Otherwise the source might stall\n    93→     * indefinitely.\n    94→     *\n    95→     * <p>It is not a problem to have occasional \"false positives\", meaning to complete a future\n    96→     * even if no data is available. However, one should not use an \"always complete\" future in\n    97→     * cases no data is available, because that will result in busy waiting loops calling {@code\n    98→     * pollNext(...)} even though no data is available.\n    99→     *\n   100→     * @return a future that will be completed once there is a record available to poll.\n   101→     */\n   102→    CompletableFuture<Void> isAvailable();\n   103→\n   104→    /**\n   105→     * Adds a list of splits for this reader to read. This method is called when the enumerator\n   106→     * assigns a split via {@link SplitEnumeratorContext#assignSplit(SourceSplit, int)} or {@link\n   107→     * SplitEnumeratorContext#assignSplits(SplitsAssignment)}.\n   108→     *\n   109→     * @param splits The splits assigned by the split enumerator.\n   110→     */\n   111→    void addSplits(List<SplitT> splits);\n   112→\n   113→    /**\n   114→     * This method is called when the reader is notified that it will not receive any further\n   115→     * splits.\n   116→     *\n   117→     * <p>It is triggered when the enumerator calls {@link\n   118→     * SplitEnumeratorContext#signalNoMoreSplits(int)} with the reader's parallel subtask.\n   119→     */\n   120→    void notifyNoMoreSplits();\n   121→\n   122→    /**\n   123→     * Handle a custom source event sent by the {@link SplitEnumerator}. This method is called when\n   124→     * the enumerator sends an event via {@link SplitEnumeratorContext#sendEventToSourceReader(int,\n   125→     * SourceEvent)}.\n   126→     *\n   127→     * <p>This method has a default implementation that does nothing, because most sources do not\n   128→     * require any custom events.\n   129→     *\n   130→     * @param sourceEvent the event sent by the {@link SplitEnumerator}.\n   131→     */\n   132→    default void handleSourceEvents(SourceEvent sourceEvent) {}\n   133→\n   134→    /**\n   135→     * We have an empty default implementation here because most source readers do not have to\n   136→     * implement the method.\n   137→     *\n   138→     * @see CheckpointListener#notifyCheckpointComplete(long)\n   139→     */\n   140→    @Override\n   141→    default void notifyCheckpointComplete(long checkpointId) throws Exception {}\n   142→\n   143→    /**\n   144→     * Pauses or resumes reading of individual source splits.\n   145→     *\n   146→     * <p>Note that no other methods can be called in parallel, so updating subscriptions can be\n   147→     * done atomically. This method is simply providing connectors with more expressive APIs the\n   148→     * opportunity to update all subscriptions at once.\n   149→     *\n   150→     * <p>This is currently used to align the watermarks of splits, if watermark alignment is used\n   151→     * and the source reads from more than one split.\n   152→     *\n   153→     * <p>The default implementation throws an {@link UnsupportedOperationException} where the\n   154→     * default implementation will be removed in future releases. To be compatible with future\n   155→     * releases, it is recommended to implement this method and override the default implementation.\n   156→     *\n   157→     * @param splitsToPause the splits to pause\n   158→     * @param splitsToResume the splits to resume\n   159→     */\n   160→    @PublicEvolving\n   161→    default void pauseOrResumeSplits(\n   162→            Collection<String> splitsToPause, Collection<String> splitsToResume) {\n   163→        throw new UnsupportedOperationException(\n   164→                \"This source reader does not support pausing or resuming splits which can lead to unaligned splits.\\n\"\n   165→                        + \"Unaligned splits are splits where the output watermarks of the splits have diverged more than the allowed limit.\\n\"\n   166→                        + \"It is highly discouraged to use unaligned source splits, as this leads to unpredictable\\n\"\n   167→                        + \"watermark alignment if there is more than a single split per reader. It is recommended to implement pausing splits\\n\"\n   168→                        + \"for this source. At your own risk, you can allow unaligned source splits by setting the\\n\"\n   169→                        + \"configuration parameter `pipeline.watermark-alignment.allow-unaligned-source-splits' to true.\\n\"\n   170→                        + \"Beware that this configuration parameter will be dropped in a future Flink release.\");\n   171→    }\n   172→}\n   173→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. RecordsWithSplitIds<E> recordsWithSplitId, ReaderOutput<T> output) throws Exception {\n   195→        // we need to loop here, in case we may have to go across splits\n   196→        while (true) {\n   197→            // Process one record.\n   198→            final E record = recordsWithSplitId.nextRecordFromSplit();\n   199→            if (record != null) {\n   200→                // emit the If nothing more is available, the next invocation will find\n   206→                // this out and return the correct status.\n   207→                // That means we emit the occasional 'false positive' for availability, but this\n   208→                // saves us doing checks for every record. Ultimately, this is cheaper.\n   209→                return trace(InputStatus.MORE_AVAILABLE);\n   210→            } else if (!moveToNextSplit(recordsWithSplitId, output)) {\n   211→                // The fetch is done and we just discovered that and have not emitted anything, yet.\n   212→                // We need to move to the next fetch. As a shortcut, we call pollNext() here again,\n   213→                // rather than emitting nothing and waiting for the caller to call us again.\n   214→                return pollNext(output);\n output) throws Exception {\n   221→        // make sure we have a fetch we are working on, or move to the next\n   222→        while (true) {\n   223→            // Check if the previous record count reached the limit of rateLimiter.\n   224→            if (!rateLimitPermissionFuture.isDone()) {\n   225→                return trace(InputStatus.MORE_AVAILABLE);\n   226→            }\n   227→ 236→                if (rateLimitingSourceOutputWrapper.getRecordsOfCurrentWindow() > 0) {\n   237→                    // Acquire permit from rateLimiter.\n   238→                    rateLimitPermissionFuture =\n   239→                            rateLimiter\n   240→                                    .acquire(\n   241→                                            rateLimitingSourceOutputWrapper\n   242→                                                    .getRecordsOfCurrentWindow())\n   243→                                    .toCompletableFuture();\n   244→                }\n   245→                rateLimitingSourceOutputWrapper.resetWindowRecordCount();\n   246→\n   247→                // We always emit MORE_AVAILABLE here, even though we do not strictly know whether\n   248→                // more is available. If nothing more is available, the next invocation will find\n   249→                // this out and return the correct status.\n   250→                // That means we emit the occasional 'false positive' for availability, but this\n   251→                // saves us doing checks for every record. return status;\n   265→    }\n   266→\n   267→    @Nullable\n   268→    private RecordsWithSplitIds<E> getNextFetch(final ReaderOutput<T> output) {\n   269→        splitFetcherManager.checkErrors();\n   270→\n   271→        LOG.trace(\"Getting next source data batch from queue\");\n   272→        final RecordsWithSplitIds<E> recordsWithSplitId = elementsQueue.poll();\n   273→        if (recordsWithSplitId == null || !moveToNextSplit(recordsWithSplitId, output)) {\n   274→            // No element available, set to available later if needed.\n   275→            return null;\n   276→        }\n   277→\n   278→        currentFetch = recordsWithSplitId;\n   279→        return recordsWithSplitId;\n   280→    }\n   281→\n   282→    private void finishCurrentFetch(\n   283→ The fetch call could be blocking\n    40→     * but it should get unblocked when {@link #wakeUp()} is invoked. In that case, the\n    41→     * implementation may either decide to return without throwing an exception, or it can just\n    42→     * throw an interrupted exception. In either case, this method should be reentrant, meaning that\n    43→     * the next fetch call should just resume from where the last fetch call was waken up or\n    44→     * interrupted. It is up to the implementer to either read all the records of the split or to\n    45→     * stop reading them at some point (for example when a given threshold is exceeded). In that\n    46→     * later case, when fetch is called again, the reading should restart at the record where it\n    47→     * left off based on the {@code SplitState}.\n    48→     *\n    49→     * @return the Ids of the finished splits.\n    50→     * @throws IOException when encountered IO errors, such as deserialization failures.\n    51→     */\n    52→    RecordsWithSplitIds<E> fetch() throws IOException;\n    53→\n    54→    /**\n    55→     * Handle the split changes. This call should be non-blocking.\n    56→     *\n    57→     * <p>For the consistency of internal state in SourceReaderBase, if an invalid split is added to\n    58→     * the reader (for example splits without any records), it should be put back into {@link\n    59→     * RecordsWithSplitIds} as finished splits so that SourceReaderBase could be able to clean up\n    60→     * resources created for it.\n    61→     *\n    62→     * <p>For the consistency of internal state in SourceReaderBase, if a split is removed, it\n    63→     * should be put back into {@link RecordsWithSplitIds} as finished splits so that\n    64→     * SourceReaderBase could be able to clean up resources created for it.\n    65→     *\n    66→     * @param splitsChanges the split changes that the SplitReader needs to handle.\n    67→     */\n    68→    void handleSplitsChanges(SplitsChange<SplitT> splitsChanges);\n    69→\n    70→    /** Wake up the split reader in case the fetcher thread is blocking in {@link #fetch()}. */\n    71→    void wakeUp();\n    72→\n    73→    /**\n    74→     * Pauses or resumes reading of individual splits readers.\n    75→     *\n    76→     * <p>Note that no other methods can be called in parallel, so it's fine to non-atomically\n    77→     * update subscriptions. This method is simply providing connectors with more expressive APIs\n    78→     * the opportunity to update all subscriptions at once.\n    79→     *\n    80→     * <p>This is currently used to align the watermarks of splits, if watermark alignment is used\n    81→     * and the source reads from more than one split.\n    82→     *\n    83→     * <p>The default implementation throws an {@link UnsupportedOperationException} where the\n    84→     * default implementation will be removed in future releases. Flink requires a type information for\n    36→ * all types that are used as input or return type of a user function. This type information class\n    37→ * acts as the tool to generate serializers and comparators, and to perform semantic checks such as\n    38→ * whether the fields that are used as join/grouping keys actually exist.\n    39→ *\n    40→ * <p>The type information also bridges between the programming languages object model and a logical\n    41→ * flat schema. It maps fields from the types to columns (fields) in a flat schema. Not all fields\n    42→ * from a type are mapped to a separate fields in the flat schema and often, entire types are mapped\n    43→ * to one field. It is important to notice that the schema must hold for all instances of a type.\n    44→ * For that reason, elements in lists and arrays are not assigned to individual fields, but the\n    45→ * lists and arrays are considered to be one field in total, to account for different lengths in the\n    46→ * arrays.\n    47→ *\n    48→ * <ul>\n    49→ *   <li>Basic types are indivisible and are considered a single field.\n    50→ *   <li>Arrays and collections are one field\n    51→ *   <li>Tuples and case classes represent as many fields as the class has fields\n    52→ * </ul>\n    53→ *\n    54→ * <p>To represent this properly, each type has an <i>arity</i> (the number of fields it contains\n    55→ * directly), and a <i>total number of fields</i> (number of fields in the entire schema of this\n    56→ * type, including nested types).\n    57→ *\n    58→ * <p>Consider the example below:\n    59→ *\n    60→ * <pre>{@code\n    61→ * public class InnerType {\n    62→ *   public int id;\n    63→ *   public String text;\n    64→ * }\n    65→ *\n    66→ * public class OuterType {\n    67→ *   public long timestamp;\n    68→ *   public InnerType nestedType;\n    69→ * }\n    70→ * }</pre>\n    71→ *\n    72→ * <p>The types \"id\", \"text\", and \"timestamp\" are basic types that take up one field. The\n    73→ * \"InnerType\" has an arity of two, and also two fields totally. The \"OuterType\" has an arity of two\n    74→ * fields, and a total number of three fields ( it contains \"id\", \"text\", and \"timestamp\" through\n    75→ * recursive flattening).\n    76→ *\n    77→ * @param <T> The type represented by this type information.\n    78→ */\n    79→@Public\n    80→public abstract class TypeInformation<T> implements Serializable {\n    81→\n    82→    private static final long serialVersionUID = -7742311969684489493L;\n    83→\n    84→    /**\n    85→     * Checks if this type information represents a basic type. Basic types are defined in {@link\n    86→     * BasicTypeInfo} and are primitives, their boxing types, Strings, Date, Void, ...\n    87→     *\n    88→     * @return True, if this type information describes a basic type, false otherwise.\n    89→     */\n    90→    @PublicEvolving\n    91→    public abstract boolean isBasicType();\n    92→\n    93→    /**\n    94→     * Checks if this type information represents a Tuple type. Tuple types are subclasses of the\n    95→     * Java API tuples.\n    96→     *\n    97→     * @return True, if this type information describes a tuple type, false otherwise.\n    98→     */\n    99→    @PublicEvolving\n   100→    public abstract boolean isTupleType();\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Different State Backends store their state in different fashions, and use different\n    42→ * data structures to hold the state of a running application.\n    43→ *\n    44→ * <p>For example, the {@link org.apache.flink.runtime.state.hashmap.HashMapStateBackend hashmap\n    45→ * state backend} keeps working state in the memory of the TaskManager. The backend is lightweight\n    46→ * and without additional dependencies.\n    47→ *\n    48→ * <p>The {@code EmbeddedRocksDBStateBackend} stores working state in an embedded <a\n    49→ * href=\"http://rocksdb.org/\">RocksDB</a> and is able to scale working state to many terabytes in\n    50→ * size, only limited by available disk space across all task managers.\n    51→ *\n    52→ * <h2>Raw Bytes Storage and Backends</h2>\n    53→ *\n    54→ * <p>The {@code StateBackend} creates services for <i>keyed state</i> and <i>operator state</i>.\n    55→ *\n    56→ * <p>The {@link CheckpointableKeyedStateBackend} and {@link OperatorStateBackend} created by this\n    57→ * state backend define how to hold the working state for keys and operators. They also define how\n    58→ * to checkpoint that state, frequently using the raw bytes storage (via the {@code\n    59→ * CheckpointStreamFactory}). However, it is also possible that for example a keyed state backend\n    60→ * simply implements the bridge to a key/value store, and that it does not need to store anything in\n    61→ * the raw byte storage upon a checkpoint.\n    62→ *\n    63→ * <h2>Serializability</h2>\n    64→ *\n    65→ * <p>State Backends need to be {@link java.io.Serializable serializable}, because they distributed\n    66→ * across parallel processes (for distributed execution) together with the streaming application\n    67→ * code.\n    68→ *\n    69→ * <p>Because of that, {@code StateBackend} implementations (typically subclasses of {@link\n    70→ * AbstractStateBackend}) are meant to be like <i>factories</i> that create the proper states stores\n    71→ * that provide access to the persistent storage and hold the keyed- and operator state data\n    72→ * structures. That way, the State Backend can be very lightweight (contain only configurations)\n    73→ * which makes it easier to be serializable.\n    74→ *\n    75→ * <h2>Thread Safety</h2>\n    76→ *\n    77→ * <p>State backend implementations have to be thread-safe. Manages the actual data fetching and emitting to the ReaderOutput. Implements non-blocking I/O semantics with availability futures.\n\n#### 3. SplitEnumerator.java Interface\n**File Path:** `/workspace/flink/flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/SplitEnumerator.java`\n\n**Key Methods/Fields:**\n- `start()` - Starts the split enumerator\n- `handleSplitRequest(int, String)` - Handles split requests from readers (with optional hostname for locality-awareness)\n- `addSplitsBack(List<SplitT>, int)` - Adds splits back when a reader fails after the last successful checkpoint\n- `addReader(int)` - Adds a new source reader with given subtask ID\n- `snapshotState(long)` - Creates a snapshot for checkpointing\n- `handleSourceEvent(int, SourceEvent)` - Handles custom source events from readers\n- `close()` - Closes the enumerator and releases resources\n\n**Role:** Discovers source splits and assigns them to SourceReaders. Runs on the JobManager side and coordinates split discovery with reader registration/failure recovery. Manages enumerator state for checkpointing.\n\n#### 4. SourceEvent.java Interface\n**File Path:** `/workspace/flink/flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/SourceEvent.java`\n\n**Key Methods/Fields:**\n- Extends `Serializable` interface\n- Marker interface for events passed between SourceReaders and Enumerators\n\n**Role:** Base interface for custom events exchanged between the reader and enumerator, enabling bidirectional communication for connector-specific protocols.\n\n#### 5. BoundedSource.java Interface\n**Status:** Not found in the repository. This interface may not exist as a separate file. Boundedness is handled via the `getBoundedness()` method in the Source interface returning a `Boundedness` enum.\n\n---\n\n### PART 2: Flink Connector Base Framework (flink-connector-base)\n\n#### 1. Handles record emission, split management, and rate limiting. Designed for efficient hand-over protocol avoiding blocking I/O in the task thread.\n\n#### 2. SplitReader.java Interface\n**File Path:** `/workspace/flink/flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/splitreader/SplitReader.java`\n\n**Key Methods/Fields:**\n- `fetch()` - Fetches elements into queue for given splits (may be blocking but should unblock with wakeUp())\n- `handleSplitsChanges(SplitsChange<SplitT>)` - Non-blocking split change handling\n- `wakeUp()` - Wakes up the split reader if blocked in fetch()\n- `pauseOrResumeSplits(Collection<SplitT>, Collection<SplitT>)` - Pauses/resumes individual splits\n\n**Role:** Low-level interface for reading from splits. Implementations handle either single or multiple splits. Manages reentrant fetch logic and split lifecycle updates.\n\n#### 3. RecordEmitter.java Interface\n**File Path:** `/workspace/flink/flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/RecordEmitter.java`\n\n**Key Methods/Fields:**\n- `emitRecord(E element, SourceOutput<T> output, SplitStateT splitState)` - Processes and emits records to downstream. Must be reentrant and idempotent if interrupted mid-emission.\n\n**Role:** Transforms intermediate elements read by SplitReader into final records emitted downstream. Handles type conversion, deserialization, and event emission with split state management.\n\n#### 4. SourceReaderManager.java\n**Status:** Not found. SplitFetcherManager.java Abstract Class\n**File Path:** `/workspace/flink/flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/fetcher/SplitFetcherManager.java`\n\n**Key Methods/Fields:**\n- `Supplier<SplitReader<E, SplitT>>` splitReaderFactory - Provides split reader instances\n- `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue<RecordsWithSplitIds<E>>` elementsQueue - Buffers fetched elements\n- `Map<Integer, SplitFetcher<E, SplitT>>` fetchers - Tracks active split fetchers\n- `ExecutorService` executors - Thread pool for fetcher and queue completion\n- `addSplits(List<SplitT>)` - Abstract method for different threading models\n- `getQueue()` - Returns the elements queue\n- `checkErrors()` - Checks for uncaught exceptions in fetchers\n- `maybeShutdownFinishedFetchers()` - Closes and removes finished fetchers\n- `pauseOrResumeSplits()` - Pauses/resumes splits across all fetchers\n\n**Role:** Manages lifecycle of SplitFetcher threads and coordinates data flow from fetchers to the blocking queue. Supports different threading models (single-thread, one-per-split) through abstract method design. Key coordinator between reader and fetchers.\n\n---\n\n### PART 3: Flink Serialization Boundary\n\n#### 1. DeserializationSchema.java Interface\n**File Path:** `/workspace/flink/flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/common/serialization/DeserializationSchema.java`\n\n**Key Methods/Fields:**\n- `open(InitializationContext)` - Initialization before deserialization\n- `deserialize(byte[] message)` - Deserializes single byte message to object\n- `deserialize(byte[] message, Collector<T> out)` - Deserializes to multiple records via Collector\n- `isEndOfStream(T nextElement)` - Determines if element signals end of stream\n- Inner interface: `InitializationContext` - Provides metric group and class loader access\n\n**Role:** Converts byte arrays from external sources (e.g., Kafka) into Java objects. Essential for bridging the binary/stream format boundary. Supports both single and multiple record emissions.\n\n#### 2. SerializationSchema.java Interface\n**File Path:** `/workspace/flink/flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/common/serialization/SerializationSchema.java`\n\n**Key Methods/Fields:**\n- `open(InitializationContext)` - Initialization before serialization\n- `serialize(T element)` - Serializes object to byte array\n- Inner interface: `InitializationContext` - Same as DeserializationSchema\n\n**Role:** Inverse of deserialization - converts Java objects to byte arrays for writing to external sinks. Used by data sinks requiring specific binary formats.\n\n#### 3. TypeInformation.java Abstract Class\n**File Path:** `/workspace/flink/flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/common/typeinfo/TypeInformation.java`\n\n**Key Methods/Fields:**\n- `isBasicType()` - Checks if this is a basic type (primitive, boxed, String, Date, Void)\n- `isTupleType()` - Checks if this is a Tuple type\n- `createTypeSerializer(SerializerConfig)` - Creates serializer for this type\n- Handles type mapping between programming language object model and flat schema\n- Provides arity (number of direct fields) and total field count information\n\n**Role:** Core Flink type system abstraction. Enables runtime serializer generation, semantic validation (key field existence), and bridging between object and schema models. All types in Flink require TypeInformation.\n\n---\n\n### PART 4: Flink Runtime Integration\n\n#### 1. SourceOperator.java Class\n**File Path:** `/workspace/flink/flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/operators/SourceOperator.java`\n\n**Key Methods/Fields:**\n- `FunctionWithException<SourceReaderContext, SourceReader<OUT, SplitT>, Exception>` sourceReaderFactory - Creates lazy-initialized reader\n- Implements `OperatorEventHandler`, `PushingAsyncDataInput<OUT>`, `WatermarkUpdateListener`\n- `SPLITS_STATE_DESC` - ListStateDescriptor for storing split state\n- Integrates with:\n  - Event handling system (AddSplitEvent, NoMoreSplitsEvent, ReaderRegistrationEvent, etc.)\n  - Checkpoint coordination (StateInitializationContext, StateSnapshotContext)\n  - Watermark strategy and alignment\n  - Metrics groups (SourceReaderMetricGroup, TaskIOMetricGroup)\n\n**Role:** Bridge between the high-level Source API (Source, SourceReader, SplitEnumerator) and Flink's streaming runtime. Manages reader lifecycle, processes coordinator events, handles state snapshots/restoration, and coordinates watermark generation.\n\n#### 2. OperatorEvent.java Interface\n**File Path:** `/workspace/flink/flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/runtime/operators/coordination/OperatorEvent.java`\n\n**Key Methods/Fields:**\n- Root interface for events sent between OperatorCoordinator and OperatorEventHandler\n- `isLossTolerant()` - Indicates if event loss is acceptable (default: false)\n\n**Role:** Base interface for operator-coordinator communication events. SourceOperator uses this to receive split assignments and other directives from the JobManager-side coordinator.\n\n#### 3. TaskStateManager.java Interface\n**File Path:** `/workspace/flink/flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/runtime/state/TaskStateManager.java`\n\n**Key Methods/Fields:**\n- `reportTaskStateSnapshots(CheckpointMetaData, CheckpointMetrics, TaskStateSnapshot, TaskStateSnapshot)` - Reports state snapshots\n- `reportIncompleteTaskStateSnapshots(CheckpointMetaData, CheckpointMetrics)` - Reports failed checkpoint stats\n- `prioritizedOperatorState(OperatorID)` - Returns previous state for operator restoration\n- `getRestoreCheckpointId()` - Acquires checkpoint ID to restore from\n- `isTaskDeployedAsFinished()` - Checks if all operators finished on restore\n\n**Role:** Manages state reporting and retrieval for task checkpoints. Coordinates between task operators and checkpoint coordinator, handling both snapshotting and restoration of operator state.\n\n#### 4. StateBackend.java Interface\n**File Path:** `/workspace/flink/flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/runtime/state/StateBackend.java`\n\n**Key Methods/Fields:**\n- `createCheckpointableKeyedStateBackend()` - Creates keyed state backend for checkpoint\n- `createOperatorStateBackend()` - Creates operator state backend\n- Thread-safe, serializable factory pattern implementation\n- Supports different backends: HashMapStateBackend, RocksDBStateBackend, etc.\n\n**Role:** Abstraction for how operator state is stored locally. Handles both working state and checkpoint persistence. Critical for source reader state management during checkpoints and recovery.\n\n---\n\n## Source Processing Pipeline Overview\n\nThe architecture follows this flow:\n\n1. **Source** (factory) creates **SplitEnumerator** (JobManager side) and **SourceReader** (task side)\n2. **SplitEnumerator** discovers splits and assigns them to readers via **OperatorEvent** messages through **SourceOperator**\n3. **SourceReader** (often via **SourceReaderBase**) receives splits and delegates to **SplitFetcherManager**\n4. **SplitFetcherManager** creates **SplitFetcher** threads that use **SplitReader** to fetch raw data\n5. **RecordEmitter** transforms raw elements using **DeserializationSchema** if needed\n6. **TypeInformation** ensures proper serialization throughout the pipeline\n7. **SourceOperator** integrates with runtime: coordinates with **TaskStateManager**, manages checkpoints via **StateBackend**, and processes **OperatorEvent**s\n8. Data flows through **ReaderOutput** to downstream operators with watermarks via **WatermarkStrategy**\n\nThis design separates concerns: enumeration logic (coordinator side), reading logic (task side), and runtime integration (operator), enabling flexible connector implementations."},{"type":"text","text":"agentId: a6c8669766ee629a7 (for resuming to continue this agent's work if needed)\n<usage>total_tokens: 49405\ntool_uses: 33\nduration_ms: 54129</usage>"}]}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"37687ef9-0768-4fe3-b674-fbdde52bf37e","uuid":"59b80811-9526-45c0-a81a-98c6d50f94fe","tool_use_result":{"status":"completed","prompt":"Explore the Apache Flink repository at /workspace/flink to find and describe the key Source API and connector framework files:\n\nPart 1 - Flink Source API (in flink-core):\n1. Data flows through **ReaderOutput** to downstream operators with watermarks via **WatermarkStrategy**\n\nThis design separates concerns: enumeration logic (coordinator side), reading logic (task side), and runtime integration (operator), enabling flexible connector implementations."}],"totalDurationMs":54129,"totalTokens":49405,"totalToolUseCount":33,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3717,"cache_read_input_tokens":41719,"output_tokens":3962,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3717,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}}}

While more lightweight interfaces exist as\n    31→ * shortcuts for various types of state, this interface offer the greatest flexibility in managing\n    32→ * both <i>keyed state</i> and <i>operator state</i>.\n    33→ *\n    34→ * <p>The section <a href=\"#shortcuts\">Shortcuts</a> illustrates the common lightweight ways to\n    35→ * setup stateful functions typically used instead of the full fledged abstraction represented by\n    36→ * this interface.\n    37→ *\n    38→ * <h1>Initialization</h1>\n    39→ *\n    40→ * <p>The {@link CheckpointedFunction#initializeState(FunctionInitializationContext)} is called when\n    41→ * the parallel instance of the transformation function is created during distributed execution. The\n    42→ * method gives access to the {@link FunctionInitializationContext} which in turn gives access to\n    43→ * the to the {@link OperatorStateStore} and {@link KeyedStateStore}.\n    44→ *\n    45→ * <p>The {@code OperatorStateStore} and {@code KeyedStateStore} give access to the data structures\n    46→ * in which state should be stored for Flink to transparently manage and checkpoint it, such as\n    47→ * {@link org.apache.flink.api.common.state.ValueState} or {@link\n    48→ * org.apache.flink.api.common.state.ListState}.\n    49→ *\n    50→ * <p><b>Note:</b> The {@code KeyedStateStore} can only be used when the transformation supports\n    51→ * <i>keyed state</i>, i.e., when it is applied on a keyed stream (after a {@code keyBy(...)}).\n    52→ *\n    53→ * <h1>Snapshot</h1>\n    54→ *\n    55→ * <p>The {@link CheckpointedFunction#snapshotState(FunctionSnapshotContext)} is called whenever a\n    56→ * checkpoint takes a state snapshot of the transformation function. Inside this method, functions\n    57→ * typically make sure that the checkpointed data structures (obtained in the initialization phase)\n    58→ * are up to date for a snapshot to be taken. The given snapshot context gives access to the\n    59→ * metadata of the checkpoint.\n    60→ *\n    61→ * <p>In addition, functions can use this method as a hook to flush/commit/synchronize with external\n    62→ * systems.\n    63→ *\n    64→ * <h1>Example</h1>\n    65→ *\n    66→ * <p>The code example below illustrates how to use this interface for a function that keeps counts\n    67→ * of events per key and per parallel partition (parallel instance of the transformation function\n    68→ * during distributed execution). The example also changes of parallelism, which affect the\n    69→ * count-per-parallel-partition by adding up the counters of partitions that get merged on\n    70→ * scale-down. Note that this is a toy example, but should illustrate the basic skeleton for a\n    71→ * stateful function.\n    72→ *\n    73→ * <pre>{@code\n    74→ * public class MyFunction<T> implements MapFunction<T, T>, CheckpointedFunction {\n    75→ *\n    76→ *     private ReducingState<Long> countPerKey;\n    77→ *     private ListState<Long> countPerPartition;\n    78→ *\n    79→ *     private long localCount;\n    80→ *\n    81→ *     public void initializeState(FunctionInitializationContext context) throws Exception {\n    82→ *         // get the state data structure for the per-key state\n    83→ *         countPerKey = context.getKeyedStateStore().getReducingState(\n    84→ *                 new ReducingStateDescriptor<>(\"perKeyCount\", new AddFunction<>(), Long.class));\n    85→ *\n    86→ *         // get the state data structure for the per-partition state\n    87→ *         countPerPartition = context.getOperatorStateStore().getOperatorState(\n    88→ *                 new ListStateDescriptor<>(\"perPartitionCount\", Long.class));\n    89→ *\n    90→ *         // initialize the \"local count variable\" based on the operator state\n    91→ *         for (Long l : countPerPartition.get()) {\n    92→ *             localCount += l;\n    93→ *         }\n    94→ *     }\n    95→ *\n    96→ *     public void snapshotState(FunctionSnapshotContext context) throws Exception {\n    97→ *         // the keyed state is always up to date anyways\n    98→ *         // just bring the per-partition state in shape\n    99→ *         countPerPartition.clear();\n   100→ *         countPerPartition.add(localCount);\n   101→ *     }\n   102→ *\n   103→ *     public T map(T value) throws Exception {\n   104→ *         // update the states\n   105→ *         countPerKey.add(1L);\n   106→ *         localCount++;\n   107→ *\n   108→ *         return value;\n   109→ *     }\n   110→ * }\n   111→ * }</pre>\n   112→ *\n   113→ * <hr>\n   114→ *\n   115→ * <h1><a name=\"shortcuts\">Shortcuts</a></h1>\n   116→ *\n   117→ * <p>There are various ways that transformation functions can use state without implementing the\n   118→ * full-fledged {@code CheckpointedFunction} interface:\n   119→ *\n   120→ * <h4>Operator State</h4>\n   121→ *\n   122→ * <p>Checkpointing some state that is part of the function object itself is possible in a simpler\n   123→ * way by directly implementing the {@link ListCheckpointed} interface.\n   124→ *\n   125→ * <h4>Keyed State</h4>\n   126→ *\n   127→ * <p>Access to keyed state is possible via the {@link RuntimeContext}'s methods:\n   128→ *\n   129→ * <pre>{@code\n   130→ * public class CountPerKeyFunction<T> extends RichMapFunction<T, T> {\n   131→ *\n   132→ *     private ValueState<Long> count;\n   133→ *\n   134→ *     public void open(OpenContext ctx) throws Exception {\n   135→ *         count = getRuntimeContext().getState(new ValueStateDescriptor<>(\"myCount\", Long.class));\n   136→ *     }\n   137→ *\n   138→ *     public T map(T value) throws Exception {\n   139→ *         Long current = count.get();\n   140→ *         count.update(current == null ? 1L : current + 1);\n   141→ *\n   142→ *         return value;\n   143→ *     }\n   144→ * }\n   145→ * }</pre>\n   146→ *\n   147→ * @see ListCheckpointed\n   148→ * @see RuntimeContext\n   149→ */\n   150→@Public\n   151→public interface CheckpointedFunction {\n   152→\n   153→    /**\n   154→     * This method is called when a snapshot for a checkpoint is requested. This acts as a hook to\n   155→     * the function to ensure that all state is exposed by means previously offered through {@link\n   156→     * FunctionInitializationContext} when the Function was initialized, or offered now by {@link\n   157→     * FunctionSnapshotContext} itself.\n   158→     *\n   159→     * @param context the context for drawing a snapshot of the operator\n   160→     * @throws Exception Thrown, if state could not be created ot restored.\n   161→     */\n   162→    void snapshotState(FunctionSnapshotContext context) throws Exception;\n   163→\n   164→    /**\n   165→     * This method is called when the parallel function instance is created during distributed\n   166→     * execution. Functions typically set up their state storing data structures in this method.\n   167→     *\n   168→     * @param context the context for initializing the operator\n   169→     * @throws Exception Thrown, if state could not be created ot restored.\n   170→     */\n   171→    void initializeState(FunctionInitializationContext context) throws Exception;\n   172→}\n   173→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.  }\n   388→\n   389→    @Override\n   390→    public void open() throws Exception {\n   391→        mainInputActivityClock = new PausableRelativeClock(getProcessingTimeService().getClock());\n   392→        TaskIOMetricGroup taskIOMetricGroup =\n   393→                getContainingTask().getEnvironment().getMetricGroup().getIOMetricGroup();\n   394→ 414→        }\n   415→\n   416→        // restore the state if necessary.\n   417→        final List<SplitT> splits = CollectionUtil.iterableToList(readerState.get());\n   418→        if      stopInternalServices();\n   440→        super.finish();\n   441→\n   442→        finished.complete(null);\n   443→    }\n   444→\n   445→    private void stopInternalServices() {\n   446→ case WAITING_FOR_ALIGNMENT:\n   457→            case OUTPUT_NOT_INITIALIZED:\n   458→            case READING:\n   459→                this.operatingMode =\n   460→                        mode == OperatingMode.SOURCE_DRAINED\n   462→                                : OperatingMode.SOURCE_STOPPED;\n   463→                availabilityHelper.forceStop();\n   464→                if (this.operatingMode == OperatingMode.SOURCE_STOPPED) {\n   465→                    stopInternalServices();\n   466→                    finished.complete(null);\n   467→                    return finished;\n   468→                }\n   469→                break;\n   470→        }\n   471→        return finished;\n   472→    }\n   473→\n   474→    @Override\n   475→    public void close() throws Exception {\n   476→        getContainingTask()\n   477→                .getEnvironment()\n   478→                .getMetricGroup()\n   479→                .getIOMetricGroup()\n   480→                .unregisterBackPressureListener(mainInputActivityClock);\n   481→\n   482→        if (sourceReader != null) {\n   483→            sourceReader.close();\n   484→        }\n   485→        super.close();\n   486→    }\n   487→\n   488→    @Override\n   489→    public DataInputStatus emitNext(DataOutput<OUT> output) throws Exception {\n   490→        // guarding an assumptions we currently make due to the fact that certain classes\n   491→        // assume a constant output, this assumption does not need to stand if we emitted all\n   492→        // records. In that case the output will change to FinishedDataOutput\n   493→        assert lastInvokedOutput == output\n   494→                || lastInvokedOutput == null\n   495→                || this.operatingMode == OperatingMode.DATA_FINISHED;\n   496→\n   497→        // short circuit the hot path. Without this short circuit (READING handled in the\n   498→        // switch/case) InputBenchmark.mapSink was showing a performance regression.\n   499→        if (operatingMode != OperatingMode.READING) {\n   500→            return emitNextNotReading(output);\n   501→        }\n   502→\n   503→        InputStatus status;\n   504→        do {\n   505→            status = sourceReader.pollNext(currentMainOutput);\n   506→        } while (status == InputStatus.MORE_AVAILABLE\n   507→                && canEmitBatchOfRecords.check()\n   508→                && !shouldWaitForAlignment());\n   509→        return convertToInternalStatus(status);\n   510→    }\n   511→\n   512→    private DataInputStatus emitNextNotReading(DataOutput<OUT> output) throws Exception {\n   513→        switch (operatingMode) {\n   514→            case OUTPUT_NOT_INITIALIZED:\n   515→                if (watermarkAlignmentParams.isEnabled()) {\n   516→                    // Only wrap the output when watermark alignment is enabled, as otherwise this\n   517→                    // introduces a small performance regression (probably because of an extra\n   518→                    // virtual call)\n   519→                    processingTimeService.scheduleWithFixedDelay(\n   520→                            time -> emitLatestWatermark(),\n   521→                            watermarkAlignmentParams.getUpdateInterval(),\n   522→                            watermarkAlignmentParams.getUpdateInterval());\n   523→                }\n   524→                initializeMainOutput(output);\n   525→                return convertToInternalStatus(sourceReader.pollNext(currentMainOutput));\n   526→            case SOURCE_STOPPED:\n   527→                this.operatingMode = OperatingMode.DATA_FINISHED;\n   528→                sourceMetricGroup.idlingStarted();\n   529→                return DataInputStatus.STOPPED;\n   530→            case SOURCE_DRAINED:\n   531→                this.operatingMode = OperatingMode.DATA_FINISHED;\n   532→                sourceMetricGroup.idlingStarted();\n   533→                return DataInputStatus.END_OF_DATA;\n   534→            case DATA_FINISHED:\n   535→                if (watermarkAlignmentParams.isEnabled()) {\n   536→                    latestWatermark = Watermark.MAX_WATERMARK.getTimestamp();\n   537→                    emitLatestWatermark();\n   538→                }\n   539→                sourceMetricGroup.idlingStarted();\n   540→                return DataInputStatus.END_OF_INPUT;\n   541→            case WAITING_FOR_ALIGNMENT:\n   542→                checkState(!waitingForAlignmentFuture.isDone());\n   543→                checkState(shouldWaitForAlignment());\n   544→                return convertToInternalStatus(InputStatus.NOTHING_AVAILABLE);\n   545→            case READING:\n   546→            default:\n   547→                throw new IllegalStateException(\"Unknown operating mode: \" + operatingMode);\n   548→        }\n   549→    }\n   550→\n   551→    private void initializeMainOutput(DataOutput<OUT> output) {\n   552→        currentMainOutput = eventTimeLogic.createMainOutput(output, this);\n   553→        initializeLatencyMarkerEmitter(output);\n   554→        lastInvokedOutput = output;\n   555→        // Create per-split output for pending splits added before main output is initialized\n   556→        createOutputForSplits(splitsToInitializeOutput);\n   557→        this.operatingMode = OperatingMode.READING;\n   558→    }\n   559→\n   560→    private void initializeLatencyMarkerEmitter(DataOutput<OUT> output) {\n   561→        long latencyTrackingInterval =\n   562→                getExecutionConfig().isLatencyTrackingConfigured()\n   563→                        ? getExecutionConfig().getLatencyTrackingInterval()\n   564→                        : getContainingTask()\n   565→                                .getEnvironment()\n   566→                                .getTaskManagerInfo()\n   567→                                .getConfiguration()\n   568→                                .get(MetricOptions.LATENCY_INTERVAL)\n   569→                                .toMillis();\n   570→        if (latencyTrackingInterval > 0) {\n   571→            latencyMarkerEmitter =\n   572→                    new LatencyMarkerEmitter<>(\n   573→                            getProcessingTimeService(),\n   574→                            output::emitLatencyMarker,\n   575→                            latencyTrackingInterval,\n   576→                            getOperatorID(),\n   577→                            getRuntimeContext().getTaskInfo().getIndexOfThisSubtask());\n   578→        }\n   579→    }\n   580→\n   581→    private DataInputStatus convertToInternalStatus(InputStatus inputStatus) {\n   582→        switch (inputStatus) {\n   583→            case MORE_AVAILABLE:\n   584→                return DataInputStatus.MORE_AVAILABLE;\n   585→            case NOTHING_AVAILABLE:\n   586→                sourceMetricGroup.idlingStarted();\n   587→                return DataInputStatus.NOTHING_AVAILABLE;\n   588→            case END_OF_INPUT:\n   589→                this.operatingMode = OperatingMode.DATA_FINISHED;\n   590→                sourceMetricGroup.idlingStarted();\n   591→                return DataInputStatus.END_OF_DATA;\n   592→            default:\n   593→                throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Unknown input status: \" + inputStatus);\n   594→        }\n   595→    }\n   596→\n   597→    private void emitLatestWatermark() {\n   598→        checkState(currentMainOutput != null);\n   599→        if (latestWatermark == Watermark.UNINITIALIZED.getTimestamp()) {\n   600→            return;\n   601→        }\n   602→        operatorEventGateway.sendEventToCoordinator(\n   603→                new ReportedWatermarkEvent(\n   604→                        idle ? Watermark.MAX_WATERMARK.getTimestamp() : latestWatermark));\n   605→    }\n   606→\n   607→    @Override\n   608→    public void snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext context) throws Exception {\n   609→     case SOURCE_DRAINED:\n   624→            case DATA_FINISHED:\n   625→                return AvailabilityProvider.AVAILABLE;\n   626→            default:\n   627→                throw new void handleOperatorEvent(OperatorEvent event) {\n   653→        if (event instanceof WatermarkAlignmentEvent) {\n   654→            updateMaxDesiredWatermark((WatermarkAlignmentEvent) event);\n   655→            checkWatermarkAlignment();\n   656→            checkSplitWatermarkAlignment();\n   657→        } else if (event instanceof AddSplitEvent) {\n   658→            handleAddSplitsEvent(((AddSplitEvent<SplitT>) event));\n   659→        } else if (event instanceof SourceEventWrapper) {\n   660→            sourceReader.handleSourceEvents(((SourceEventWrapper) event).getSourceEvent());\n   661→        } else if (event instanceof NoMoreSplitsEvent) {\n   662→            sourceReader.notifyNoMoreSplits();\n   663→        } else if (event instanceof IsProcessingBacklogEvent) {\n   664→            if (eventTimeLogic != null) {\n   665→                eventTimeLogic.emitImmediateWatermark(System.currentTimeMillis());\n   666→            }\n   667→            output.emitRecordAttributes(\n   668→                    new RecordAttributesBuilder(Collections.emptyList())\n   669→                            .setBacklog(((IsProcessingBacklogEvent) event).isProcessingBacklog())\n   670→                            .build());\n   671→        } else {\n   672→            throw new IllegalStateException(\"Received unexpected operator event \" + event);\n   673→        }\n   674→    }\n   675→\n   676→    private void handleAddSplitsEvent(AddSplitEvent<SplitT> event) {\n   677→        try {\n   678→            List<SplitT> newSplits = event.splits(splitSerializer);\n   679→            if (operatingMode == OperatingMode.OUTPUT_NOT_INITIALIZED) {\n   680→                // For splits arrived before the main output is initialized, store them into the\n   681→                // pending list. Outputs of these splits will be created once the main output is\n   682→                // ready.\n   683→                splitsToInitializeOutput.addAll(newSplits);\n   684→            } else {\n   685→                // Create output directly for new splits if the main output is already initialized.\n   686→                createOutputForSplits(newSplits);\n   687→            }\n   688→            sourceReader.addSplits(newSplits);\n   689→            createMetricGroupForSplits(newSplits);\n   690→        } catch (IOException e) {\n   691→            throw new FlinkRuntimeException(\"Failed to deserialize the splits.\", e);\n   692→        }\n   693→    }\n   694→\n   695→    private void createOutputForSplits(List<SplitT> newSplits) {\n   696→        for (SplitT split : newSplits) {\n   697→            currentMainOutput.createOutputForSplit(split.splitId());\n   698→        }\n   699→    }\n   700→\n   701→    private void createMetricGroupForSplits(List<SplitT> newSplits) {\n   702→        for (SplitT split : newSplits) {\n   703→            getOrCreateSplitMetricGroup(split.splitId());\n   704→        }\n   705→    }\n   706→\n   707→    private void updateMaxDesiredWatermark(WatermarkAlignmentEvent event) {\n   708→        currentMaxDesiredWatermark = event.getMaxWatermark();\n   709→        sourceMetricGroup.updateMaxDesiredWatermark(currentMaxDesiredWatermark);\n   710→    }\n   711→\n   712→    @Override\n   713→    public void updateIdle(boolean isIdle) {\n   714→        this.idle = isIdle;\n   715→    }\n   716→\n   717→    @Override\n   718→    public void updateCurrentEffectiveWatermark(long watermark) {\n   719→        latestWatermark = watermark;\n   720→        checkWatermarkAlignment();\n   721→    }\n   722→\n   723→    @Override\n   724→    public void updateCurrentSplitWatermark(String splitId, long watermark) {\n   725→        splitCurrentWatermarks.put(splitId, watermark);\n   726→        if (watermark > currentMaxDesiredWatermark && !currentlyPausedSplits.contains(splitId)) {\n   727→            pauseOrResumeSplits(Collections.singletonList(splitId), Collections.emptyList());\n   728→            currentlyPausedSplits.add(splitId);\n   729→        }\n   730→    }\n   731→\n   732→    @Override\n   733→    public void updateCurrentSplitIdle(String splitId, boolean idle) {\n   734→        if (idle) {\n   735→            this.getOrCreateSplitMetricGroup(splitId).markIdle();\n   736→        } else {\n   737→            this.getOrCreateSplitMetricGroup(splitId).markNotIdle();\n   738→        }\n   739→    }\n   740→\n   741→    @Override\n   742→    public void splitFinished(String splitId) {\n   743→        splitCurrentWatermarks.remove(splitId);\n   744→        getOrCreateSplitMetricGroup(splitId).onSplitFinished();\n   745→        this.splitMetricGroups.remove(splitId);\n   746→    }\n   747→\n   748→    /**\n   749→     * Finds the splits that are beyond the current max watermark and pauses them. At the same time,\n   750→     * splits that have been paused and where the global watermark caught up are resumed.\n   751→     *\n   752→     * <p>Note: This takes effect only if there are multiple splits, otherwise it does nothing.\n   753→     */\n   754→    private void checkSplitWatermarkAlignment() {\n   755→        Collection<String> splitsToPause = new ArrayList<>();\n   756→        Collection<String> splitsToResume = new ArrayList<>();\n   757→        splitCurrentWatermarks.forEach(\n   758→                (splitId, splitWatermark) -> {\n   759→                    if (splitWatermark > currentMaxDesiredWatermark) {\n   760→                        splitsToPause.add(splitId);\n   761→                    } else if (currentlyPausedSplits.contains(splitId)) {\n   762→                        splitsToResume.add(splitId);\n   763→                    }\n   764→                });\n   765→        splitsToPause.removeAll(currentlyPausedSplits);\n   766→        if (!splitsToPause.isEmpty() || !splitsToResume.isEmpty()) {\n   767→            pauseOrResumeSplits(splitsToPause, splitsToResume);\n   768→            currentlyPausedSplits.addAll(splitsToPause);\n   769→            splitsToResume.forEach(currentlyPausedSplits::remove);\n   770→        }\n   771→    }\n   772→\n   773→    private void pauseOrResumeSplits(\n   774→            Collection<String>  793→        }\n   794→    }\n   795→\n   796→    private void checkWatermarkAlignment() {\n   797→        if (operatingMode == OperatingMode.READING) {\n   798→ OperatingMode.READING;\n   808→                waitingForAlignmentFuture.complete(null);\n   809→                mainInputActivityClock.unPause();\n   810→            }\n   811→        }\n   812→    }\n   813→\n   814→    private boolean shouldWaitForAlignment() {\n   815→        return currentMaxDesiredWatermark < latestWatermark;\n   816→    }\n   817→\n   818→    private void Typical examples\n    64→     * would be Logs, PubSubs, or Message Queues, like Kafka or Kinesis, which store a timestamp\n    65→     * with each event.\n    66→     *\n    67→     * <p>The events typically still pass through a {@link TimestampAssigner}, which may decide to\n    68→     * either use this source-provided timestamp, or replace it with a timestamp stored within the\n    69→     * event (for example if the event was a JSON object one could configure aTimestampAssigner that\n    70→     * extracts one of the object's fields and uses that as a timestamp).\n    71→     *\n    72→     * @param record the record to emit.\n    73→     * @param timestamp the timestamp of the record.\n    74→     */\n    75→    @Override\n    76→    void collect(T record, long timestamp);\n    77→\n    78→    /**\n    79→     * Emits the given watermark.\n    80→     *\n    81→     * <p>Emitting a watermark also implicitly marks the stream as <i>active</i>, ending previously\n    82→     * marked idleness.\n    83→     */\n    84→    @Override\n    85→    void emitWatermark(Watermark watermark);\n    86→\n    87→    /**\n    88→     * Marks this output as idle, meaning that downstream operations do not wait for watermarks from\n    89→     * this output.\n    90→     *\n    91→     * <p>An output becomes active again as soon as the next watermark is emitted.\n    92→     */\n    93→    @Override\n    94→    void markIdle();\n    95→\n    96→    /**\n    97→     * Creates a {@code SourceOutput} for a specific Source Split. doing so. Instead, emit one record into the ReaderOutput and return a {@link\n    69→     * InputStatus#MORE_AVAILABLE} to let the caller thread know there are more records available.\n    70→     *\n    71→     * @return The InputStatus of the SourceReader after the method invocation.\n    72→     */\n    73→    InputStatus pollNext(ReaderOutput<T> output) throws Exception;\n    74→\n    75→    /**\n    76→     * Checkpoint on the state of the source.\n    77→     *\n    78→     * @return the state of the source.\n    79→     */\n    80→    List<SplitT> snapshotState(long checkpointId);\n    81→\n    82→    /**\n    83→     * Returns a future that signals that data is available from the reader.\n    84→     *\n    85→     * <p>Once the future completes, the runtime will keep calling the {@link\n    86→     * #pollNext(ReaderOutput)} method until that method returns a status other than {@link\n    87→     * InputStatus#MORE_AVAILABLE}. After that, the runtime will again call this method to obtain\n    88→     * the next future. Otherwise the source might stall\n    93→     * indefinitely.\n    94→     *\n    95→     * <p>It is not a problem to have occasional \"false positives\", meaning to complete a future\n    96→     * even if no data is available. The OperatorCoordinator runs on the master, associated with\n    37→ * the job vertex of the operator. It communicates with operators via sending operator events.\n    38→ *\n    39→ * <p>Operator coordinators are for example source and sink coordinators that discover and assign\n    40→ * work, or aggregate and commit metadata.\n    41→ *\n    42→ * <h2>Thread Model</h2>\n    43→ *\n    44→ * <p>All coordinator methods are called by the Job Manager's main thread (mailbox thread). That\n    45→ * means that these methods must not, under any circumstances, perform blocking operations (like I/O\n    46→ * or waiting on locks or futures). That would run a high risk of bringing down the entire\n    47→ * JobManager.\n    48→ *\n    49→ * <p>Coordinators that involve more complex operations should hence spawn threads to handle the I/O\n    50→ * work. The methods on the {@link Context} are safe to be called from another thread than the\n    51→ * thread that calls the Coordinator's methods.\n    52→ *\n    53→ * <h2>Consistency</h2>\n    54→ *\n    55→ * <p>The coordinator's view of the task execution is highly simplified, compared to the Scheduler's\n    56→ * view, but allows for consistent interaction with the operators running on the parallel subtasks.\n    57→ * In particular, the following methods are guaranteed to be called strictly in order:\n    58→ *\n    59→ * <ol>\n    60→ *   <li>{@link #executionAttemptReady(int, int, SubtaskGateway)}: Called once you can send events\n    61→ *       to the subtask execution attempt. The provided gateway is bound to that specific execution\n    62→ *       attempt. This is the start of interaction with the operator subtask attempt.\n    63→ *   <li>{@link #executionAttemptFailed(int, int, Throwable)}: Called for each subtask execution\n    64→ *       attempt as soon as the attempt failed or was cancelled. At this point, interaction with the\n    65→ *       subtask attempt should stop.\n    66→ *   <li>{@link #subtaskReset(int, long)} or {@link #resetToCheckpoint(long, byte[])}: Once the\n    67→ *       scheduler determined which checkpoint to restore, these methods notify the coordinator of\n    68→ *       that. The former method is called in case of a regional failure/recovery (affecting\n    69→ *       possible a subset of subtasks), the later method in case of a global failure/recovery. This\n    70→ *       method should be used to determine which actions to recover, because it tells you which\n    71→ *       checkpoint to fall back to. The coordinator implementation needs to recover the\n    72→ *       interactions with the relevant tasks since the checkpoint that is restored. It will be\n    73→ *       called only after {@link #executionAttemptFailed(int, int, Throwable)} has been called on\n    74→ *       all the attempts of the subtask.\n    75→ *   <li>{@link #executionAttemptReady(int, int, SubtaskGateway)}: Called again, once the recovered\n    76→ *       tasks (new attempts) are ready to go. This is later than {@link #subtaskReset(int, long)},\n    77→ *       because between those methods, the new attempts are scheduled and deployed.\n    78→ * </ol>\n    79→ */\n    80→@Internal\n    81→public interface OperatorCoordinator extends CheckpointListener, AutoCloseable {\n    82→\n    83→    /**\n    84→     * The checkpoint ID passed to the restore methods when no completed checkpoint exists, yet. It\n    85→     * indicates that the restore is to the \"initial state\" of the coordinator or the failed\n    86→     * subtask.\n    87→     */\n    88→    long NO_CHECKPOINT = -1L;\n    89→\n    90→    /** The checkpoint ID passed to the restore methods when batch scenarios. */\n    91→    long BATCH_CHECKPOINT_ID = -1L;\n    92→\n    93→    // ------------------------------------------------------------------------\n    94→\n    95→    /**\n    96→     * Starts the coordinator. This method is called once at the beginning, before any other\n    97→     * methods.\n    98→     *\n    99→     * @throws Exception Any exception thrown from this method causes a full job failure.\n   100→     */\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
